<p><b>Luxembourg</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/ʌ/: &#39;u&#39; in &#39;cut&#39;">ʌ</span><span title="&#39;k&#39; in &#39;kind&#39;">k</span><span title="&#39;s&#39; in &#39;sigh&#39;">s</span><span title="/əm/: &#39;m&#39; in &#39;rhythm&#39;">əm</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="/ɜːr/: &#39;ur&#39; in &#39;fur&#39;">ɜːr</span><span title="/ɡ/: &#39;g&#39; in &#39;guy&#39;">ɡ</span></span>/</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Luxembourg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7a/En-us-Luxembourg.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Luxembourg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small></span>) (<a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourgish language">Luxembourgish</a>: <i lang="lb">Lëtzebuerg</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Luxembourgish" title="Help:IPA/Luxembourgish">[ˈlətsəbuə̯ɕ]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Lb-L%C3%ABtzebuerg.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/42/Lb-L%C3%ABtzebuerg.ogg" class="internal" title="Lb-Lëtzebuerg.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Luxembourg</i>&#160;; <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Luxemburg</i>), officially the <b>Grand Duchy of Luxembourg</b>,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;note 2&#93;</a></sup> is a small <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in western Europe. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> to the west and north, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> to the east, and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to the south. Its capital, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>, together with <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>, is one of the three official capitals of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and the seat of the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a>, the highest judicial authority in the EU. Its culture, people, and languages are highly intertwined with its neighbours, making it essentially a mixture of <a href="/wiki/French_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="French culture">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="German culture">German</a> cultures, as evident by the nation's three <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official languages</a>: <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish" title="Luxembourgish">Luxembourgish</a> (sometimes considered a dialect of German). The repeated invasions by Germany, especially in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_in_World_War_II" title="Luxembourg in World War II">World War II</a>, resulted in the country's strong will for mediation between France and Germany and, among other things, led to the foundation of the European Union.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With an area of 2,586 square kilometres (998&#160;sq&#160;mi), it is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_area" title="List of European countries by area">smallest sovereign states in Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-europa1_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-europa1-10">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, Luxembourg had a population of 576,249, which makes it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population" title="List of European countries by population">least-populous countries in Europe</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> but by far the one with the <a href="/wiki/List_of_European_countries_by_population_growth_rate" title="List of European countries by population growth rate">highest population growth rate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Foreigners account for nearly half of Luxembourg's population.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> As a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarch</a>, it is headed by <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Henri" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke Henri">Grand Duke Henri</a> and is the world's only remaining <a href="/wiki/Grand_duchy" title="Grand duchy">grand duchy</a>. Luxembourg is a <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">developed country</a>, with an advanced economy and one of the world's highest <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">GDP (PPP) per capita</a>. The City of Luxembourg with its old quarters and fortifications was declared a <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1994 due to the exceptional preservation of the vast fortifications and the old city.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The history of Luxembourg is considered to begin in 963, when count <a href="/wiki/Sigfried,_Count_of_the_Ardennes" title="Sigfried, Count of the Ardennes">Siegfried I</a> acquired a rocky promontory and its Roman-era fortifications known as <i>Lucilinburhuc</i>, ′little castle′, and the surrounding area from the <a href="/wiki/St._Maximin%27s_Abbey,_Trier" title="St. Maximin&#39;s Abbey, Trier">Imperial Abbey of St. Maximin</a> in nearby <a href="/wiki/Trier" title="Trier">Trier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
Siegfried's descendants increased their territory through marriage, war and vassal relations. At the end of the 13th century, the <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Counts of Luxembourg">Counts of Luxembourg</a> reigned over a considerable territory.
<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
In 1308, <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry VII, Holy Roman Emperor">Henry VII, Count of Luxembourg</a> became <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Germans" class="mw-redirect" title="King of the Germans">King of the Germans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a>. The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Luxembourg" title="House of Luxembourg">House of Luxembourg</a> produced four <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperors" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Roman Emperors">Holy Roman Emperors</a> at the high time of the Middle Ages. In 1354, <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles IV, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles IV</a> elevated the County to the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Duchy of Luxembourg">Duchy of Luxembourg</a>. Since <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund</a> had no male heir, the Duchy became part of the <a href="/wiki/Burgundian_Circle" title="Burgundian Circle">Burgundian Circle</a> and then one of the <a href="/wiki/Seventeen_Provinces" title="Seventeen Provinces">Seventeen Provinces</a> of the Habsburg Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
Over the centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Luxembourg" title="Fortress of Luxembourg">City and Fortress of Luxembourg</a>, of great strategic importance situated between the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburg</a> territories, was gradually built up to be one of the most reputed <a href="/wiki/Fortifications" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortifications">fortifications</a> in Europe. After belonging to both the France of <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis XIV">Louis XIV</a> and the Austria of <a href="/wiki/Maria_Theresia" class="mw-redirect" title="Maria Theresia">Maria Theresia</a>, Luxembourg became part of the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="First French Republic">First French Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">Empire</a> under <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The present-day state of Luxembourg first emerged at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> in 1815. The Grand-Duchy, with its powerful fortress, became an independent state under the personal possession of <a href="/wiki/William_I_of_the_Netherlands" title="William I of the Netherlands">William I of the Netherlands</a> with a <a href="/wiki/Prussian" class="mw-redirect" title="Prussian">Prussian</a> garrison to guard the city against another invasion from France.
<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
In 1839, following the turmoil of the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a>, the purely Oil-speaking part of Luxembourg was ceded to <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and the Luxembourgish-speaking part (except the <a href="/wiki/Arelerland" title="Arelerland">Arelerland</a>, the area around <a href="/wiki/Arlon" title="Arlon">Arlon</a>) became what is the present state of Luxembourg.
<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Steel_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Steel industry">steel industry</a> exploiting the <a href="/wiki/Red_Lands" title="Red Lands">Red Lands</a>' rich iron-ore grounds in the beginning of the 20th century drove the country's industrialisation. <a href="/wiki/ArcelorMittal" title="ArcelorMittal">ArcelorMittal</a>, the world's largest steel producer with headquarters in Luxembourg City, is still a reminder of these times. After the decline of the steel industry in the 1970s, the country focused on establishing itself as a global financial centre and developed into the banking hub it is reputed for. Since the beginning of the 21st century, its governments have focused on developing the country into a <a href="/wiki/Knowledge_economy" title="Knowledge economy">knowledge economy</a>, with the founding of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Luxembourg" title="University of Luxembourg">University of Luxembourg</a> and a national <a href="/wiki/Space_programme" class="mw-redirect" title="Space programme">space programme</a>, projecting the first involvement in a robotic lunar expedition by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luxembourg is a founding member of the European Union, <a href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">OECD</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>, <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>. The city of Luxembourg, which is the country's capital and largest city, is the seat of several institutions and agencies of the EU. Luxembourg served on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">United Nations Security Council</a> for the years 2013 and 2014, which was a first in the country's history.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In 2016 Luxembourgish citizens had visa-free or visa-on-arrival access to 172 countries and territories, ranking the Luxembourgish passport 15th in the world, tied with countries such as Canada and Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Luxembourg" title="History of Luxembourg">History of Luxembourg</a></div>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="County">County</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: County">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/County_of_Luxemburg" title="County of Luxemburg">County of Luxemburg</a></div>
<p>The recorded history of Luxembourg begins with the acquisition of Lucilinburhuc<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> (today <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Castle" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg Castle">Luxembourg Castle</a>) situated on the <a href="/wiki/Bock_(Luxembourg)" title="Bock (Luxembourg)">Bock</a> rock by <a href="/wiki/Siegfried_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Siegfried of Luxembourg">Siegfried, Count of Ardennes</a>, in 963 through an exchange act with <a href="/wiki/St._Maximin%27s_Abbey,_Trier" title="St. Maximin&#39;s Abbey, Trier">St. Maximin's Abbey, Trier</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Around this <a href="/wiki/Fortifications" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortifications">fort</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Town" title="Town">town</a> gradually developed, which became the centre of a state of great strategic value.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Duchy">Duchy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Duchy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Luxemburg" title="Duchy of Luxemburg">Duchy of Luxemburg</a></div>
<p>In the 14th and early 15th centuries, three members of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Luxembourg" title="House of Luxembourg">House of Luxembourg</a> reigned as <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperors</a>. In 1437, the House of Luxembourg suffered a succession crisis, precipitated by the lack of a male heir to assume the throne, which led to the territories being sold by Duchess <a href="/wiki/Elisabeth,_Duchess_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Elisabeth, Duchess of Luxembourg">Elisabeth</a> to <a href="/wiki/Philip_the_Good" title="Philip the Good">Philip the Good</a> of <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Burgundy" title="Duchy of Burgundy">Burgundy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the following centuries, Luxembourg's fortress was steadily enlarged and strengthened by its successive occupants, the <a href="/wiki/Bourbons" class="mw-redirect" title="Bourbons">Bourbons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Habsburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Habsburg">Habsburgs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern" class="mw-redirect" title="Hohenzollern">Hohenzollerns</a> and the French.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nineteenth_century">Nineteenth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Nineteenth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1815)" title="Treaty of Paris (1815)">defeat</a> of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> in 1815, Luxembourg was disputed between <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="United Kingdom of the Netherlands">Netherlands</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a> formed Luxembourg as a <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duchy">Grand Duchy</a> within the German Confederation. The Dutch king became, in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>, the grand duke. Although he was supposed to rule the grand duchy as an independent country with an administration of its own, in reality he treated it similarly to a Dutch province. The <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Luxembourg" title="Fortress of Luxembourg">Fortress of Luxembourg</a> was manned by Prussian troops for the German Confederation.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> This arrangement was revised by the 1839 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London,_1839" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of London, 1839">First Treaty of London</a>, from which date Luxembourg's full independence is reckoned.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg/220px-Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg/330px-Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg/440px-Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxemburg-Petrussetal-Viaduc.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luxembourg City: The Passerelle, also known as the viaduct or old bridge, overlooking the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9trusse" title="Pétrusse">Pétrusse</a> river valley; it opened in 1861.</div></div></div>
<p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Belgian_Revolution" title="Belgian Revolution">Belgian Revolution</a> of 1830–1839, and by the 1839 Treaty establishing full independence, Luxembourg's territory was reduced by more than half, as the predominantly <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">francophone</a> <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(Belgium)" title="Luxembourg (Belgium)">western part of the country</a> was transferred to <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. In 1842 Luxembourg joined the German Customs Union (<a href="/wiki/Zollverein" title="Zollverein">Zollverein</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> This resulted in the opening of the German market, the development of <a href="/wiki/Steel_industry_in_Luxembourg" title="Steel industry in Luxembourg">Luxembourg's steel industry</a>, and expansion of <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_Nationale_des_Chemins_de_Fer_Luxembourgeois" title="Société Nationale des Chemins de Fer Luxembourgeois">Luxembourg's railway network</a> from 1855 to 1875, particularly the construction of the Luxembourg-<a href="/wiki/Thionville" title="Thionville">Thionville</a> railway line, with connections from there to the European industrial regions.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> While Prussian troops still manned the fortress, in 1861, the <a href="/wiki/Passerelle_(Luxembourg)" title="Passerelle (Luxembourg)">Passerelle</a> was opened, the first road bridge spanning the <a href="/wiki/P%C3%A9trusse" title="Pétrusse">Pétrusse</a> river valley, connecting the <a href="/wiki/Ville_Haute" title="Ville Haute">Ville Haute</a> and the main fortification on the Bock with <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_railway_station" title="Luxembourg railway station">Luxembourg railway station</a>, opened in 1859, on the then fortified Bourbon plateau to the south.
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Crisis" title="Luxembourg Crisis">Luxembourg Crisis</a> of 1866 nearly led to war between Prussia and France, the Grand Duchy's independence and neutrality were again affirmed by the 1867 <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_London,_1867" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of London, 1867">Second Treaty of London</a>, Prussia's troops were withdrawn from the Fortress of Luxembourg, and its Bock and surrounding fortifications were dismantled.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Netherlands" class="mw-redirect" title="King of the Netherlands">King of the Netherlands</a> remained <a href="/wiki/Head_of_State" class="mw-redirect" title="Head of State">Head of State</a> as <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Grand Duke of Luxembourg</a>, maintaining a personal union between the two countries until 1890. At the death of <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_the_Netherlands" title="William III of the Netherlands">William III</a>, the throne of the Netherlands passed to his daughter <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_of_the_Netherlands" title="Wilhelmina of the Netherlands">Wilhelmina</a>, while Luxembourg (then restricted to male heirs by the <a href="/wiki/Nassau_Family_Pact" title="Nassau Family Pact">Nassau Family Pact</a>) passed to <a href="/wiki/Adolphe,_Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" title="Adolphe, Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Adolph of Nassau-Weilburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the time of the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Franco-Prussian war">Franco-Prussian war</a> in 1870, despite allegations about French use of the Luxembourg railways for passing soldiers from <a href="/wiki/Metz" title="Metz">Metz</a> (then part of France) through the Duchy, and for forwarding provisions to Thionville, Luxembourg's neutrality was respected by <a href="/wiki/North_German_Confederation" title="North German Confederation">Germany</a>, and neither France nor Germany invaded the country.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> But in 1871, as a result of Germany's victory over France, Luxembourg's boundary with <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(duchy)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorraine (duchy)">Lorraine</a>, containing Metz and Thionville, changed from being a frontier with a part of France to a frontier with territory annexed to the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> as <a href="/wiki/Alsace-Lorraine" title="Alsace-Lorraine">Alsace-Lorraine</a> under the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Frankfurt_(1871)" title="Treaty of Frankfurt (1871)">Treaty of Frankfurt</a>. This allowed Germany the military advantage of controlling and expanding the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Railways_in_Alsace-Lorraine" title="Imperial Railways in Alsace-Lorraine">railways there</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg_(city)_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg/220px-Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg" width="220" height="99" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg/330px-Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg/440px-Luxembourg_%28city%29_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5006" data-file-height="2257" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg_(city)_-_view_from_Metz_square.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>View to Place de la Constitution and <a href="/wiki/G%C3%ABlle_Fra" title="Gëlle Fra">Gëlle Fra</a> monument, from <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg (city)">the capital's Metz square</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Adolphe_Bridge" title="Adolphe Bridge">Adolphe Bridge</a> end of <a href="/wiki/Avenue_de_la_Libert%C3%A9" title="Avenue de la Liberté">Avenue de la Liberté</a>, connecting with the railway station</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Twentieth_century">Twentieth century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Twentieth century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alsace-lorraine.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alsace-lorraine.JPG/150px-Alsace-lorraine.JPG" width="150" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alsace-lorraine.JPG/225px-Alsace-lorraine.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Alsace-lorraine.JPG/300px-Alsace-lorraine.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1701" data-file-height="2262" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alsace-lorraine.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Frontier with German Empire's Alsace-Lorraine, from 1871 to 1918</div></div></div>
<p>In August 1914, <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Germany">Imperial Germany</a> violated Luxembourg's neutrality in the war by invading it in the war against France. This allowed Germany to use the railway lines, while at the same time denying them to France. Nevertheless, despite the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Luxembourg_during_World_War_I" title="German occupation of Luxembourg during World War I">German occupation</a>, Luxembourg was allowed to maintain much of its independence and political mechanisms.
</p><p>In 1940, after the outbreak of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, Luxembourg's neutrality was again violated when the <a href="/wiki/Wehrmacht" title="Wehrmacht">Wehrmacht</a> of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> entered the country, "entirely without justification".<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> In contrast to the First World War, under the <a href="/wiki/German_occupation_of_Luxembourg_during_World_War_II" title="German occupation of Luxembourg during World War II">German occupation of Luxembourg during World War II</a>, the country was treated as German territory and informally annexed to the adjacent province of the <a href="/wiki/Third_Reich" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Reich">Third Reich</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_government-in-exile" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg government-in-exile">government in exile</a> based in London supported the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a>, sending a small group of volunteers who participated in the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Normandy" title="Invasion of Normandy">Normandy invasion</a>. Luxembourg was liberated in September 1944, and became a founding member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in 1945. Luxembourg's neutral status under the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Luxembourg" title="Constitution of Luxembourg">constitution</a> formally ended in 1948, and in 1949 it became a founding member of <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>.
</p><p>In 1951, Luxembourg became one of the six founding countries of the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>, which in 1957 would become the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> and in 1993 the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. In 1999 Luxembourg joined the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a>. In 2005, a <a href="/wiki/Referendum_on_EU_treaty_in_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Referendum on EU treaty in Luxembourg">referendum on the EU treaty establishing a constitution for Europe</a> was held.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Luxembourg" title="Politics of Luxembourg">Politics of Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Luxembourg" title="Law of Luxembourg">Law of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Ducal_Palace,_Luxembourg_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg/220px-Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg" width="220" height="130" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg/330px-Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg/440px-Grand_Ducal_Palace%2C_Luxembourg_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1696" data-file-height="1003" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_Ducal_Palace,_Luxembourg_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Grand_Ducal_Palace,_Luxembourg" title="Grand Ducal Palace, Luxembourg">Grand Ducal Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>, the official residence of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Grand Duke of Luxembourg</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG/220px-Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG/330px-Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG/440px-Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Hall of the Chamber of Deputies, the meeting place of the Luxembourgish national legislature, the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Luxembourg">Chamber of Deputies</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a></div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg is a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> headed by a <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarch</a>. Under the constitution of 1868, executive power is exercised by the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke of Luxembourg">Grand Duke</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a>, which consists of several other ministers.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The Grand Duke has the power to dissolve the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_(Luxembourg)" title="Chamber of Deputies (Luxembourg)">legislature</a>, in which case new elections must be held within three months. However, since 1919, sovereignty has resided with the <a href="/wiki/Nation" title="Nation">Nation</a>, exercised by the Grand Duke in accordance with the Constitution and the law.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Legislative power is vested in the <a href="/wiki/Chamber_of_Deputies_of_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Chamber of Deputies of Luxembourg">Chamber of Deputies</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicameral">unicameral</a> legislature of sixty members, who are directly elected to five-year terms from four <a href="/wiki/Legislative_circonscriptions_(Luxembourg)" title="Legislative circonscriptions (Luxembourg)">constituencies</a>. A second body, the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_State_of_Luxembourg" title="Council of State of Luxembourg">Council of State</a> (<i>Conseil d'État</i>), composed of twenty-one ordinary citizens appointed by the Grand Duke, advises the Chamber of Deputies in the drafting of legislation.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Grand Duchy has three lower tribunals (<i>justices de paix</i>; in <a href="/wiki/Esch-sur-Alzette" title="Esch-sur-Alzette">Esch-sur-Alzette</a>, the city of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Diekirch" title="Diekirch">Diekirch</a>), two district tribunals (Luxembourg and Diekirch), and a <a href="/wiki/Superior_court_of_justice_(Luxembourg)" class="mw-redirect" title="Superior court of justice (Luxembourg)">Superior Court of Justice</a> (Luxembourg), which includes the Court of Appeal and the Court of Cassation. There is also an Administrative Tribunal and an Administrative Court, as well as a Constitutional Court, all of which are located in the capital.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Luxembourg" title="Cantons of Luxembourg">Cantons of Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Luxembourg" title="Communes of Luxembourg">Communes of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Luxembourg" title="Administrative divisions of Luxembourg">Administrative divisions of Luxembourg</a></div>
<p>Luxembourg is divided into 12 <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_Luxembourg" title="Cantons of Luxembourg">cantons</a>, which are further divided into 102 <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_Luxembourg" title="Communes of Luxembourg">communes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Twelve of the communes have <a href="/wiki/List_of_cities_in_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="List of cities in Luxembourg">city status</a>, of which the city of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a> is the largest.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional center">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png/91px-LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png" width="91" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png/137px-LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png/183px-LuxembourgPartitionsMap_english.png 2x" data-file-width="433" data-file-height="569" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>The three <a href="/wiki/Partitions_of_Luxembourg" title="Partitions of Luxembourg">Partitions of Luxembourg</a> greatly reduced Luxembourg's territory.
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:15px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png/90px-Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png" width="90" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png/135px-Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png/180px-Groothertogdom_LuxemburgKantons.png 2x" data-file-width="203" data-file-height="270" /></a></div></div>

</p>
