</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Luxembourg" title="Foreign relations of Luxembourg">Foreign relations of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_(1674586821).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/220px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/330px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg/440px-European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_%281674586821%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:European_Court_of_Justice_-_Luxembourg_(1674586821).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a>, seated in <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg City</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg has long been a prominent supporter of European political and <a href="/wiki/Economic_integration" title="Economic integration">economic integration</a>. In efforts foreshadowing European integration, Luxembourg and Belgium in 1921 formed the <a href="/wiki/Belgium%E2%80%93Luxembourg_Economic_Union" title="Belgium–Luxembourg Economic Union">Belgium–Luxembourg Economic Union</a> (BLEU) to create a regime of inter-exchangeable currency and a common <a href="/wiki/Customs_(tax)" class="mw-redirect" title="Customs (tax)">customs</a>. Luxembourg is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Benelux_Economic_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Benelux Economic Union">Benelux Economic Union</a> and was one of the founding members of the European Economic Community (now the European Union). It also participates in the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Agreement" title="Schengen Agreement">Schengen Group</a> (named after <a href="/wiki/Schengen,_Luxembourg" title="Schengen, Luxembourg">the Luxembourg village of Schengen</a> where the agreements were signed), whose goal is the free movement of citizens among member states. At the same time, the majority of Luxembourgers have consistently believed that European unity makes sense only in the context of a dynamic transatlantic relationship, and thus have traditionally pursued a pro-<a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>, pro-US foreign policy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p><p>Luxembourg is the site of the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">European Court of Justice</a>, the <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Auditors" title="European Court of Auditors">European Court of Auditors</a>, the Statistical Office of the European Communities ("<a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">Eurostat</a>") and other vital EU organs. The <a href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_the_European_Parliament" title="Secretariat of the European Parliament">Secretariat of the European Parliament</a> is located in Luxembourg, but the Parliament usually meets in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> and sometimes in <a href="/wiki/Strasbourg" title="Strasbourg">Strasbourg</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Army" title="Luxembourg Army">Luxembourg Army</a></div><p>The Army is situated on the "Härebierg" which is Luxemburgish and translates to "men's mountain".<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nato_awacs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Nato_awacs.jpg/220px-Nato_awacs.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Nato_awacs.jpg/330px-Nato_awacs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Nato_awacs.jpg/440px-Nato_awacs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1123" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nato_awacs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a>-owned <a href="/wiki/Boeing_E-3_Sentry" title="Boeing E-3 Sentry">AWACS</a> aircraft</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg maintains a very small army of about 800 soldiers and 100 civil servants to its defense and to NATO. Being a landlocked country, it has no navy.
</p><p>Luxembourg also lacks an air force, though the 17 NATO <a href="/wiki/Airborne_Warning_And_Control_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Airborne Warning And Control System">AWACS</a> aeroplanes are, for convenience, registered as aircraft of Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-Aeroflight_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aeroflight-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> In accordance with a joint agreement with Belgium, both countries have put forth funding for one <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A400M" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A400M">A400M</a> military cargo plane.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Luxembourg" title="Geography of Luxembourg">Geography of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Luxembourg-CIA_WFB_Map.png/220px-Luxembourg-CIA_WFB_Map.png" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/15/Luxembourg-CIA_WFB_Map.png 1.5x" data-file-width="326" data-file-height="350" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg-CIA_WFB_Map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The largest towns are <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(city)" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg (city)">Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esch-sur-Alzette" title="Esch-sur-Alzette">Esch-sur-Alzette</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dudelange" title="Dudelange">Dudelange</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Differdange" title="Differdange">Differdange</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg is one of the smallest countries in Europe, and ranked <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_area" class="mw-redirect" title="List of countries by area">169th</a> in size of all the <a href="/wiki/List_of_sovereign_states" title="List of sovereign states">194 independent countries of the world</a>; the country is about 2,586 square kilometres (998&#160;sq&#160;mi) in size, and measures 82&#160;km (51&#160;mi) long and 57&#160;km (35&#160;mi) wide. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/49th_parallel_north" title="49th parallel north">49°</a> and <a href="/wiki/51st_parallel_north" title="51st parallel north">51° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/5th_meridian_east" title="5th meridian east">5°</a> and <a href="/wiki/7th_meridian_east" title="7th meridian east">7° E</a> <sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To the east, Luxembourg borders the German <i><a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">Bundesländer</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Rhineland-Palatinate" title="Rhineland-Palatinate">Rhineland-Palatinate</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a>, and to the south, it borders the French <i><a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9gion_in_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Région in France">région</a></i> of <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorraine (region)">Lorraine</a>. The Grand Duchy borders the Belgian <a href="/wiki/Wallonia" title="Wallonia">Walloon Region</a>, in particular the latter's <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_regions_in_Belgium" class="mw-redirect" title="Provinces of regions in Belgium">provinces</a> of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_(Belgium)" title="Luxembourg (Belgium)">Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Li%C3%A8ge_(province)" title="Liège (province)">Liège</a>, part of which comprises the <a href="/wiki/German-speaking_Community_of_Belgium" title="German-speaking Community of Belgium">German-speaking Community of Belgium</a>, to the west and to the north, respectively.
</p><p>The northern third of the country is known as the '<a href="/wiki/Oesling" title="Oesling">Oesling</a>', and forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Ardennes" title="Ardennes">Ardennes</a>. It is dominated by hills and low mountains, including the <a href="/wiki/Kneiff" title="Kneiff">Kneiff</a> near Wilwerdange,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> which is the highest point, at 560 metres (1,837&#160;ft). Other mountains are the '<a href="/wiki/Buurgplaatz" title="Buurgplaatz">Buurgplaaz</a>' at 559 metres near <a href="/wiki/Huldange" title="Huldange">Huldange</a> and the '<a href="/wiki/Napol%C3%A9onsgaard" title="Napoléonsgaard">Napoléonsgaard</a>' at 554 metres near <a href="/wiki/Rambrouch" title="Rambrouch">Rambrouch</a>. The region is sparsely populated, with only one town (<a href="/wiki/Wiltz" title="Wiltz">Wiltz</a>) with a population of more than four thousand people.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Clerve_Alscheid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Clerve_Alscheid.jpg/220px-Clerve_Alscheid.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Clerve_Alscheid.jpg/330px-Clerve_Alscheid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Clerve_Alscheid.jpg/440px-Clerve_Alscheid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Clerve_Alscheid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Typical Luxembourg countryside near <a href="/wiki/Alscheid" title="Alscheid">Alscheid</a></div></div></div>
<p>The southern two-thirds of the country is called the "<a href="/wiki/Gutland_(Luxembourg)" title="Gutland (Luxembourg)">Gutland</a>", and is more densely populated than the Oesling. It is also more diverse and can be divided into five geographic sub-regions. The <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_plateau" title="Luxembourg plateau">Luxembourg plateau</a>, in south-central Luxembourg, is a large, flat, <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">sandstone</a> formation, and the site of the city of Luxembourg. <a href="/wiki/Little_Switzerland_(Luxembourg)" title="Little Switzerland (Luxembourg)">Little Switzerland</a>, in the east of Luxembourg, has craggy terrain and thick forests. The <a href="/wiki/Moselle_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moselle (river)">Moselle</a> valley is the lowest-lying region, running along the southeastern border. The <a href="/wiki/Red_Lands" title="Red Lands">Red Lands</a>, in the far south and southwest, are Luxembourg's industrial heartland and home to many of Luxembourg's largest towns.
</p><p>The border between Luxembourg and Germany is formed by three <a href="/wiki/River" title="River">rivers</a>: the Moselle, the <a href="/wiki/Sauer" title="Sauer">Sauer</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Our_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Our River">Our</a>. Other major rivers are the <a href="/wiki/Alzette" title="Alzette">Alzette</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Attert_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Attert River">Attert</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Clerve" title="Clerve">Clerve</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Wiltz_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Wiltz River">Wiltz</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Valley" title="Valley">valleys</a> of the mid-Sauer and Attert form the border between the Gutland and the Oesling.
</p><p>According to the 2012 Environmental Performance Index, Luxembourg is one of the world's best performers in environmental protection, ranking 4th out of 132 assessed countries<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Luxembourg also ranks 6th among the top ten most livable cities in the world by Mercer's.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luxembourg has an <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen</a>: Cfb), marked by high precipitation, particularly in late summer. The summers are warm and winters cool.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Luxembourg" title="Economy of Luxembourg">Economy of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/170px-Eurozone.svg.png" width="170" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/255px-Eurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/340px-Eurozone.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="450" data-file-height="456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luxembourg is part of the <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen Area</a>, the EU single market, and the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> (dark blue)</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg_treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Luxembourg_treemap.png/220px-Luxembourg_treemap.png" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Luxembourg_treemap.png/330px-Luxembourg_treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Luxembourg_treemap.png/440px-Luxembourg_treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="1108" data-file-height="868" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Luxembourg_treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Graphical depiction of Luxembourg's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG/220px-Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG/330px-Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG/440px-Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Spuerkeess_headquarters_2012-04.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Banque_et_Caisse_d%27%C3%89pargne_de_l%27%C3%89tat" title="Banque et Caisse d&#39;Épargne de l&#39;État">Banque et Caisse d'Épargne de l'État</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a></div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg's stable and high-income <a href="/wiki/Economic_system" title="Economic system">market economy</a> features moderate <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth</a>, low <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>, and a high level of innovation.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Unemployment is traditionally low, although it had risen to 6.1% by May 2012, due largely to the effect of the <a href="/wiki/2008_global_financial_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 global financial crisis">2008 global financial crisis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Consequently, Luxembourg's economy was forecast to have negligible growth in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, according to the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (PPP) per capita">IMF</a>, Luxembourg was the second richest country in the world, with a per capita GDP on a purchasing-power parity (PPP) basis of $80,119.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> Luxembourg is ranked 13th in <a href="/wiki/The_Heritage_Foundation" title="The Heritage Foundation">The Heritage Foundation</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Index_of_Economic_Freedom" title="Index of Economic Freedom">Index of Economic Freedom</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> 26th in the United Nations <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a>, and 4th in the Economist Intelligence Unit's <a href="/wiki/Quality-of-life_index" class="mw-redirect" title="Quality-of-life index">quality of life index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>External debt of Luxembourg is $14,385,000,000, or a per capital debt of $24,308. The debt to GDP is 23%. <sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The industrial sector, which was dominated by steel until the 1960s, has since diversified to include chemicals, rubber, and other products. During the past decades, growth in the financial sector has more than compensated for the decline in <a href="/wiki/Steel_industry_in_Luxembourg" title="Steel industry in Luxembourg">steel production</a>. Services, especially banking and <a href="/wiki/Financial_export" class="mw-redirect" title="Financial export">finance</a>, account for the majority of economic output. Luxembourg is the world's second largest investment fund centre (after the United States), the most important private banking centre in the <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">Eurozone</a> and Europe's leading centre for reinsurance companies. Moreover, the Luxembourg government has aimed to attract Internet start-ups, with <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon.com">Amazon</a> being two of the many Internet companies that have shifted their regional headquarters to Luxembourg.
</p><p>In April 2009, concern about Luxembourg's banking secrecy laws, as well as its reputation as a <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a>, led to its being added to a "grey list" of nations with questionable banking arrangements by the <a href="/wiki/G20" title="G20">G20</a>. In response, the country soon after adopted OECD standards on exchange of information and was subsequently added into the category of "jurisdictions that have substantially implemented the internationally agreed tax standard".<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> In March 2010, the <i>Sunday Telegraph</i> reported that most of Kim Jong-Il's $4 billion in secret accounts is in Luxembourg banks.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Amazon.co.uk also benefits from Luxembourg tax loopholes by channeling substantial UK revenues as reported by <i>The Guardian</i> in April 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> Luxembourg ranked third on the <a href="/wiki/Tax_Justice_Network" title="Tax Justice Network">Tax Justice Network</a>'s 2011 <a href="/wiki/Financial_Secrecy_Index" title="Financial Secrecy Index">Financial Secrecy Index</a> of the world's major tax havens, scoring only slightly behind the <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">Cayman Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, Luxembourg is ranked as the 2nd safest tax haven in the world, behind <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.
</p><p>Agriculture is based on small, family-owned farms.
</p><p>Luxembourg has especially close trade and financial ties to Belgium and the Netherlands (see <a href="/wiki/Benelux" title="Benelux">Benelux</a>), and as a member of the EU it enjoys the advantages of the open European <a href="/wiki/Market_(economics)" title="Market (economics)">market</a>.
</p><p>With $171 billion in May 2015, the country ranks eleventh in the world in holdings of <a href="/wiki/U.S._Treasury_security" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Treasury security">U.S. Treasury securities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> However, securities owned by non-Luxembourg residents, but held in custodial accounts in Luxembourg, are also included in this figure.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Luxembourg" title="Transport in Luxembourg">Transport in Luxembourg</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/History_of_rail_transport_in_Luxembourg" title="History of rail transport in Luxembourg">History of rail transport in Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg/220px-LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg/330px-LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg/440px-LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LUX_Check-In_Schalter.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Luxembourg's international airline <a href="/wiki/Luxair" title="Luxair">Luxair</a> is based at <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Airport" title="Luxembourg Airport">Luxembourg Airport</a>, the country's only international airport.</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg has efficient road, rail and air transport facilities and services. The road network has been significantly modernised in recent years with 147&#160;km (91&#160;mi) of motorways connecting the capital to adjacent countries. The advent of the high-speed <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGV</a> link to Paris has led to renovation of the city's <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_railway_station" title="Luxembourg railway station">railway station</a> and a new passenger terminal at <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Airport" title="Luxembourg Airport">Luxembourg Airport</a> was opened in 2008. Luxembourg city reintroduced <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Luxembourg" title="Trams in Luxembourg">trams</a> in December 2017 and there are plans to open <a href="/wiki/Light-rail" class="mw-redirect" title="Light-rail">light-rail</a> lines in adjacent areas within the next few years.
</p><p>The number of cars per 1000 persons amount to 680.1 in Luxembourg — higher than all but two <a href="/wiki/State_(polity)" title="State (polity)">states</a>, namely the <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Principality of Monaco</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">British overseas territory of Gibraltar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The telecommunications industry in Luxembourg is liberalised and the electronic communications networks are significantly developed. Competition between the different operators is guaranteed by the legislative framework Paquet Telecom<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> of the Government of 2011 which transposes the European Telecom Directives into Luxembourgish law. This encourages the investment in networks and services. The regulator ILR – Institut Luxembourgeois de Régulation<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> ensures the compliance to these legal rules.
</p><p>Luxembourg has modern and widely deployed optical fiber and cable networks throughout the country. In 2010, the Luxembourg Government launched its National strategy for very high-speed networks with the aim to become a global leader in terms of very high-speed broadband by achieving full 1 Gbit/s coverage of the country by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Luxembourg had an <a href="/wiki/Next-generation_access" class="mw-redirect" title="Next-generation access">NGA</a> coverage of 75%.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In April 2013, Luxembourg featured the 6th highest download speed worldwide and the 2nd highest in Europe: 32,46 Mbit/s.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The country's location in Central Europe, stable economy and low taxes favour the telecommunication industry.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It ranks 2nd in the world in the development of the Information and Communication Technologies in the ITU ICT Development Index and 8th in the Global Broadband Quality Study 2009 by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oviedo" title="University of Oviedo">University of Oviedo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg/220px-Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg/330px-Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg/440px-Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3782" data-file-height="2790" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Centre_Drosbach_Luxembourg_Signs_-_June_2012.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Signs in front of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Centre_Drosbach&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Centre Drosbach (page does not exist)">Centre Drosbach</a> on the Cloche d'or, in the city of <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City" title="Luxembourg City">Luxembourg</a></div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg is connected to all major European Internet Exchanges (AMS-IX Amsterdam,<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> DE-CIX Frankfurt,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> LINX London),<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> datacenters and POPs through redundant optical networks.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In addition, the country is connected to the virtual meetme room services (vmmr)<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> of the international data hub operator Ancotel.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> This enables Luxembourg to interconnect with all major telecommunication operators<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> and data carriers worldwide. The interconnection points are in Frankfurt, London, New York and Hong Kong.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several providers interconnect Luxembourg to the major European data hubs:
</p>
<ul><li>Teralink<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/P%26TLuxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="P&amp;TLuxembourg">P&amp;TLuxembourg</a>, also called EPT Luxembourg: incumbent operator)<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/LuxConnect" title="LuxConnect">LuxConnect</a><sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> (shareholder&#160;: Government) LuxConnect tested the 100G coherent transmission of data signals between Luxembourg and Amsterdam in June 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Artelis/Cegecom<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> (alternative telecommunications provider in Luxembourg and Saarland)</li>
<li>Satellite connectivity – Teleports (<a href="/wiki/SES_S.A." title="SES S.A.">SES</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> Broadcasting Center Europe<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and P&amp;T Luxembourg Teleport.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Luxembourg is connected through an optical <a href="/wiki/DWDM" class="mw-redirect" title="DWDM">DWDM</a> network, called Teralink<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> to several Tier 1 upstream providers like Level3 and Global Crossing. Teralink offers connectivities up to 100 Gbit/s. P&amp;TLuxembourg established a coherent 100Gbit/s IP connection between Frankfurt and Luxembourg with live traffic in 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Internet IPV6 protocol has been introduced to the country by Restena and P&amp;T Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luxembourg has one <a href="/wiki/Internet_exchange_point" title="Internet exchange point">Internet exchange point</a> and one Carrier <a href="/wiki/Ethernet_Exchange" title="Ethernet Exchange">Ethernet Exchange</a> point.
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_Commercial_Internet_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourg Commercial Internet Exchange">LU-CIX</a> is Luxembourg's neutral and commercial Internet Exchange Point which was founded in 2009 by Cegecom, Datacentre Luxembourg, Global Media Systems, INEXIO, LuxConnect, P&amp;T Luxembourg and Root eSolutions. It offers a short, fast and efficient route to the major European Internet networks.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In 2012, LIX, the neutral Internet exchange operated by the RESTENA Foundation, merged with LU-CIX.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> In March 2013, LU-CIX launched the 'Central European Peering Hub' in order to provide the opportunity to its members to connect to other IXs' reseller programs, AMS-IX (Amsterdam), LINX (London), DE-CIX (Frankfurt) and France-IX (Paris), etc.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg_Ethernet_Exchange&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Luxembourg Ethernet Exchange (page does not exist)">LIX</a> is the Luxembourg Ethernet Exchange located in the Tier IV certified eBRC datacentre.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The online portal De Guichet<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> of the Grand Duchy of Luxembourg is a single one-stop online shop for citizens and companies to undertake various administrative operations (procedures, online forms, downloadable forms, and advice) by Internet.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" class="mw-redirect" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">PSA Peugeot Citroën</a>, with <a href="/wiki/P%26TLuxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="P&amp;TLuxembourg">P&amp;TLuxembourg</a> as its partner, has introduced an integrated mobile telecommunication solution for the development of its telematic services in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Data_centres">Data centres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Data centres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Some 20 data centres<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> are operating in Luxembourg. Six data centers are Tier IV Design certified: three of ebrc,<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup> two of LuxConnect <sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> and one of European Data Hub.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> In a survey on nine international data centers carried out in December 2012 and January 2013 and measuring availability (up-time) and performance (delay by which the data from the requested website was received), the top three positions were held by Luxembourg data centers.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="FinTech">FinTech</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: FinTech">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Luxembourg has established itself as one of the leading <a href="/wiki/Financial_technology" title="Financial technology">financial technology</a> (FinTech) hubs in Europe, with the Luxembourg government supporting initiatives like the Luxembourg House of Financial Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Luxembourg" title="Demographics of Luxembourg">Demographics of Luxembourg</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnicity">Ethnicity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnicity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The people of Luxembourg are called <a href="/wiki/Luxembourger" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourger">Luxembourgers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> population increased in the 20th century due to the arrival of immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, with the majority coming from the latter: in 2013 there were about 88,000 inhabitants with <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Luxembourger" title="Portuguese Luxembourger">Portuguese</a> nationality.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> In 2013, there were 537,039 permanent residents, 44.5% of which were of foreign background or foreign nationals; the largest foreign ethnic groups were the Portuguese, comprising 16.4% of the total population, followed by the French (6.6%), Italians (3.4%), Belgians (3.3%) and Germans (2.3%). Another 6.4% were of other <a href="/wiki/EU" class="mw-redirect" title="EU">EU</a> background, while the remaining 6.1% were of other non-EU, but largely other European, background.<sup id="cite_ref-statnews13_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-statnews13-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Yugoslav_wars" class="mw-redirect" title="Yugoslav wars">Yugoslav wars</a>, Luxembourg has seen many immigrants from <a href="/wiki/Bosnia_and_Herzegovina" title="Bosnia and Herzegovina">Bosnia and Herzegovina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>. Annually, over 10,000 new immigrants arrive in Luxembourg, mostly from the EU states, as well as <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">Eastern Europe</a>. In 2000 there were 162,000 immigrants in Luxembourg, accounting for 37% of the total population. There were an estimated 5,000 illegal immigrants in Luxembourg in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Largest Groups of Immigrants:<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ol><li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal"><img alt="Portugal" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/45px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> (100,460)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> (38,384)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy"><img alt="Italy" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/23px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/35px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/03/Flag_of_Italy.svg/45px-Flag_of_Italy.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="1000" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> (21,877)</li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:LUX-5f2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LUX-5f2.jpg/220px-LUX-5f2.jpg" width="220" height="111" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/LUX-5f2.jpg/330px-LUX-5f2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7e/LUX-5f2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="407" data-file-height="206" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:LUX-5f2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coin of the former <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_franc" title="Luxembourgish franc">Luxembourg franc</a> in two of the country's three languages: French (obverse, left) and Luxembourgish (reverse, right)</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Luxembourg" title="Languages of Luxembourg">Languages of Luxembourg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism_in_Luxembourg" title="Multilingualism in Luxembourg">Multilingualism in Luxembourg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_literature" title="Luxembourg literature">Luxembourg literature</a></div>
<p>The linguistic situation of Luxemburg is complex. It is characterized by the existence of a language specific to the local population (<a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourgish Language">Luxembourgish</a>), mixed with the historical presence of the two major languages spoken in the surrounding countries (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>).
</p><p>Three languages are recognised as official in Luxembourg: <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Luxembourgish language">Luxembourgish</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Franconian_languages" title="Franconian languages">Franconian</a> language of the <a href="/wiki/Moselle_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moselle (river)">Moselle</a> region that is also spoken in neighbouring parts of Belgium, Germany and France. Though Luxembourgish is part of the West Central German group of <a href="/wiki/High_German_languages" title="High German languages">High German languages</a>, more than 5,000 words in the language are of French origin.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> The first printed sentences in Luxembourgish appeared in a weekly journal, the 'Luxemburger Wochenblatt', in the second edition on 14 April 1821.
</p><p>Apart from being one of the three official languages, Luxembourgish is also considered the <a href="/wiki/National_language" title="National language">national language</a> of the Grand Duchy; it is the mother tongue or "language of the heart" for the local population.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to the historical influence of the Napoleonic Code on the legal system of the Grand Duchy, French is the sole language of the legislation. 
</p><p>French is generally the preferred language of the government, administration and justice. The parliamentary debates are however mostly conducted in Luxembourgish, whereas the written government communications and the official documents (e.g. administrative or judicial decisions, passports etc.) are drafted only in French.
</p><p>Every resident has the right to address the administration in the language of their choice among the three official languages, and to be answered in that language.
</p><p>In the everyday life, road signs are only in French, written communications to the public are either only in French or in both French and Luxembourgish, while German is much more present in the media, alongside with French.
</p><p>Each of the three languages is used as the primary language in certain spheres, without being exclusive. Luxembourgish is the language that Luxembourgers generally use to speak to each other, but it is not often used as the written language. Since the 1980s, however, an increasing number of novels have been written in Luxembourgish. Most official business is carried out in French. German is very often used in much of the <a href="/wiki/Mass_media" title="Mass media">media</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>. 
</p><p>Among the numerous expatriate workers, French seems to be the <i>lingua franca</i>, alongside with English in some sectors.
</p><p>Luxembourg is member of the <a href="/wiki/Francophonie_(organisation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophonie (organisation)">International Organisation of the Francophonie</a>.
</p><p>According to a recent survey, French is the language spoken by most residents (99%), followed by Luxembourgish (82%), German (81%) and English (72%)<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>. 
</p><p>Although professional life is largely multilingual, French is described by private sector business leaders as the main working language of their company (56%), followed by Luxembourgish (20%), English (18%) and German (6%)<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>. 
</p><p>Luxembourg's education system is trilingual: the first years of primary school are in German, before changing to Luxembourgish; while in secondary school, the language of instruction changes to French.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Proficiency in all three languages is required for graduation from secondary school, but half the students leave school without a certified qualification, with the children of immigrants being particularly disadvantaged.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the three national languages, English is taught in compulsory schooling and much of the population of Luxembourg can speak English. The past two decades have highlighted the growing importance of English in several sectors, in particular the financial sector. Portuguese, the language of the largest immigrant community, is also spoken by large segments of the population, but by relatively few from outside the Portuguese-speaking community.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><br />
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Luxembourg" title="Religion in Luxembourg">Religion in Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG/150px-Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG/225px-Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG/300px-Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Notre_Dame_Cathedral_Luxembourg.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame_Cathedral,_Luxembourg" title="Notre-Dame Cathedral, Luxembourg">Notre-Dame Cathedral</a>, Luxembourg City</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg is a <a href="/wiki/Secular_state" title="Secular state">secular state</a>, but the state recognises certain religions as officially mandated religions. This gives the state a hand in religious administration and appointment of clergy, in exchange for which the state pays certain running costs and wages. Currently, religions covered by such arrangements are <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholicism">Roman Catholicism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Judaism" title="Judaism">Judaism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greek_Orthodoxy" class="mw-redirect" title="Greek Orthodoxy">Greek Orthodoxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglicanism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Orthodox_Church" title="Russian Orthodox Church">Russian Orthodoxy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutheranism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Calvinism" title="Calvinism">Calvinism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mennonitism" class="mw-redirect" title="Mennonitism">Mennonitism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1980 it has been illegal for the government to collect statistics on religious beliefs or practices.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> An estimation by the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA Factbook</a> for the year 2000 is that 87% of Luxembourgers are <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>, including the grand ducal family, the remaining 13% being made up of <a href="/wiki/Protestants" class="mw-redirect" title="Protestants">Protestants</a>, <a href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christians" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthodox Christians">Orthodox Christians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">Jews</a>, Muslims, and those of other or no religion.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_World_Factbook_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA_World_Factbook-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> According to a 2010 <a href="/wiki/Pew_Research_Center" title="Pew Research Center">Pew Research Center</a> study 70.4% are Christian, 2.3% Muslim, 26.8% unaffiliated and 0.5% other religions.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2005 <a href="/wiki/Eurobarometer" title="Eurobarometer">Eurobarometer</a> poll,<sup id="cite_ref-EUROBAROMETER_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-EUROBAROMETER-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> 44% of Luxembourg citizens responded that "they believe there is a <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a>", whereas 28% answered that "they believe there is some sort of spirit or life force" and 22% that "they do not believe there is any sort of spirit, god, or life force".
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg/220px-University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg/330px-University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg/440px-University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:University_luxemburg_lmp_main.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Luxembourg" title="University of Luxembourg">University of Luxembourg</a> is the only university based in the country.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_secondary_schools_in_Luxembourg" title="List of secondary schools in Luxembourg">List of secondary schools in Luxembourg</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Luxembourg" title="University of Luxembourg">University of Luxembourg</a> is the only university based in Luxembourg. Two American universities maintain campuses in the country, the <a href="/wiki/Miami_University_Dolibois_European_Center" title="Miami University Dolibois European Center">Miami University Dolibois European Center</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sacred_Heart_University_Luxembourg" title="Sacred Heart University Luxembourg">Sacred Heart University Luxembourg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Luxembourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Health in Luxembourg">Health in Luxembourg</a></div>
<p>Luxembourg sells the most alcohol in Europe per capita.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> However, the large proportion of alcohol purchased by customers from neighboring countries contributes to the statistically high level of alcohol sales per capita; this level of alcohol sales is thus not representative of the actual alcohol consumption of the Luxembourg population.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Luxembourg" title="Culture of Luxembourg">Culture of Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_symbols_of_Luxembourg" title="National symbols of Luxembourg">National symbols of Luxembourg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_Steichen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Edward_Steichen.jpg/170px-Edward_Steichen.jpg" width="170" height="320" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Edward_Steichen.jpg/255px-Edward_Steichen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Edward_Steichen.jpg/340px-Edward_Steichen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="698" data-file-height="1315" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Edward_Steichen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Edward_Steichen" title="Edward Steichen">Edward Steichen</a>, Luxembourgish photographer and painter</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg has been overshadowed by the culture of its neighbours. It retains a number of folk traditions, having been for much of its history a profoundly rural country. There are several notable museums, located mostly in the capital. These include the <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_History_and_Art" title="National Museum of History and Art">National Museum of History and Art</a> (NMHA), the <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_City_History_Museum" title="Luxembourg City History Museum">Luxembourg City History Museum</a>, and the new <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duke_Jean_Museum_of_Modern_Art" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Duke Jean Museum of Modern Art">Grand Duke Jean Museum of Modern Art</a> (Mudam). The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Military_History_(Luxembourg)" title="National Museum of Military History (Luxembourg)">National Museum of Military History (MNHM)</a> in Diekirch is especially known for its representations of the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Bulge" title="Battle of the Bulge">Battle of the Bulge</a>. The city of Luxembourg itself is on the <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_List" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage List">World Heritage List</a>, on account of the historical importance of its fortifications.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country has produced some internationally known artists, including the painters <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9o_Kerg" title="Théo Kerg">Théo Kerg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Kutter" title="Joseph Kutter">Joseph Kutter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michel_Majerus" title="Michel Majerus">Michel Majerus</a>, and photographer <a href="/wiki/Edward_Steichen" title="Edward Steichen">Edward Steichen</a>, whose <i><a href="/wiki/The_Family_of_Man" title="The Family of Man">The Family of Man</a></i> exhibition has been placed on UNESCO's <a href="/wiki/Memory_of_the_World_Programme" title="Memory of the World Programme">Memory of the World</a> register, and is now permanently housed in <a href="/wiki/Clervaux" title="Clervaux">Clervaux</a>. Movie star <a href="/wiki/Loretta_Young" title="Loretta Young">Loretta Young</a> was of Luxembourgish descent.
</p><p>Luxembourg was the first city to be named <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> twice. The first time was in 1995. In 2007, the European Capital of Culture<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> was to be a cross-border area consisting of the Grand Duchy of Luxembourg, the Rheinland-Pfalz and Saarland in Germany, the Walloon Region and the German-speaking part of Belgium, and the <a href="/wiki/Lorraine_(region)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lorraine (region)">Lorraine</a> area in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. The event was an attempt to promote mobility and the exchange of ideas, crossing borders physically, psychologically, artistically and emotionally.
</p><p>Luxembourg was represented at the World <a href="/wiki/Expo_2010" title="Expo 2010">Expo 2010</a> in Shanghai, China, from 1 May to 31 October 2010 with its own pavilion.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> The pavilion was based on the transliteration of the word Luxembourg into Chinese, "Lu Sen Bao", which means "Forest and Fortress". It represented Luxembourg as the "Green Heart in Europe".<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Charly_Gaul_1959_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Charly_Gaul_1959_%28cropped%29.jpg/180px-Charly_Gaul_1959_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="180" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Charly_Gaul_1959_%28cropped%29.jpg/270px-Charly_Gaul_1959_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/74/Charly_Gaul_1959_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="352" data-file-height="510" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Charly_Gaul_1959_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Charly Gaul won three <a href="/wiki/Grand_Tour_(cycling)" title="Grand Tour (cycling)">Grand Tours</a> in his cycling career.</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Luxembourg" title="Sport in Luxembourg">Sport in Luxembourg</a></div>
<p>Unlike most countries in Europe, sport in Luxembourg is not concentrated upon a particular <a href="/wiki/National_sport" title="National sport">national sport</a>, but encompasses a number of sports, both team and individual. Despite the lack of a central sporting focus, over 100,000 people in Luxembourg, out of a total population of near 500,000–600,000, are licensed members of one sports federation or another.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> The largest sports venue in the country is <a href="/wiki/D%27Coque" title="D&#39;Coque">d'Coque</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Indoor_arena" class="mw-redirect" title="Indoor arena">indoor arena</a> and Olympic swimming pool in <a href="/wiki/Kirchberg,_Luxembourg" title="Kirchberg, Luxembourg">Kirchberg</a>, north-eastern Luxembourg City, which has a capacity of 8,300. The arena is used for basketball, handball, gymnastics, and volleyball, including the final of the <a href="/wiki/2007_Women%27s_European_Volleyball_Championship" title="2007 Women&#39;s European Volleyball Championship">2007 Women's European Volleyball Championship</a>. The <a href="/wiki/National_stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="National stadium">national stadium</a> (also the country's largest) is the <a href="/wiki/Stade_Josy_Barthel" title="Stade Josy Barthel">Stade Josy Barthel</a>, in western Luxembourg City; named after the country's only official Olympic gold medallist, the stadium has a capacity of 8,054.
</p><p>Notable sportspeople include (see also <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Luxembourgish_Sportspeople_of_the_Year" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Luxembourgish Sportspeople of the Year">List of Luxembourgish Sportspeople of the Year</a></i>):
</p>
<ul><li>Alpine skier <a href="/wiki/Marc_Girardelli" title="Marc Girardelli">Marc Girardelli</a>, <a href="/wiki/FIS_Alpine_Ski_World_Cup" title="FIS Alpine Ski World Cup">World Cup</a> overall champion five times between 1985 and 1993</li>
<li>Cyclists <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Frantz" title="Nicolas Frantz">Nicolas Frantz</a>, winner of the 1927 and 1928 <a href="/wiki/Tours_de_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Tours de France">Tours de France</a>; <a href="/wiki/Charly_Gaul" title="Charly Gaul">Charly Gaul</a>, winner of the 1956 and 1959 <a href="/wiki/Giro_d%27Italia" title="Giro d&#39;Italia">Giro d'Italia</a> and of the 1958 <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a>; <a href="/wiki/Elsy_Jacobs" title="Elsy Jacobs">Elsy Jacobs</a>, first ever <a href="/wiki/UCI_Road_World_Championships_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_road_race" title="UCI Road World Championships – Women&#39;s road race">women's Road World Champion</a> in 1958; and <a href="/wiki/Andy_Schleck" title="Andy Schleck">Andy Schleck</a>, winner of the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Tour_de_France" title="Tour de France">Tour de France</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Middle-distance_runner" class="mw-redirect" title="Middle-distance runner">Middle-distance runner</a> <a href="/wiki/Josy_Barthel" title="Josy Barthel">Josy Barthel</a>, winner of the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_1952_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_1500_metres" title="Athletics at the 1952 Summer Olympics – Men&#39;s 1500 metres">men's 1500 metres at the 1952 Summer Olympics</a></li>
<li>1961 <a href="/wiki/World_water_skiing_champion" class="mw-redirect" title="World water skiing champion">world water skiing champion</a> <a href="/wiki/Sylvie_H%C3%BClsemann" title="Sylvie Hülsemann">Sylvie Hülsemann</a></li>
<li>Tennis players <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Muller" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilles Muller">Gilles Muller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Kremer" title="Anne Kremer">Anne Kremer</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mandy_Minella" title="Mandy Minella">Mandy Minella</a>.</li>
<li>Football player <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Strasser" title="Jeff Strasser">Jeff Strasser</a>, played in the German <a href="/wiki/Bundesliga" title="Bundesliga">Bundesliga</a> from 1999–2006.</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg_cuisine" title="Luxembourg cuisine">Luxembourg cuisine</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG/150px-JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG/225px-JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG/300px-JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:JuddMatGaardebounen_Beer.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i><a href="/wiki/Judd_mat_Gaardebounen" title="Judd mat Gaardebounen">Judd mat Gaardebounen</a></i>, served with boiled potatoes and <a href="/wiki/Diekirch" title="Diekirch">Diekirch</a> beer</div></div></div>
<p>Luxembourg cuisine reflects its position on the border between the Latin and Germanic worlds, being heavily influenced by the cuisines of neighboring France and Germany. More recently, it has been enriched by its many Italian and Portuguese immigrants.
</p><p>Most native Luxembourg dishes, consumed as the traditional daily fare, share roots in the country's folk dishes the same as in neighboring <a href="/wiki/German_cuisine" title="German cuisine">Germany</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Luxembourg&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main languages of media in Luxembourg are French and German. The newspaper with the largest circulation is the German-language daily <i><a href="/wiki/Luxemburger_Wort" title="Luxemburger Wort">Luxemburger Wort</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>. Because of the strong multilingualism in Luxembourg, newspapers often alternate articles in French and articles in German, without translation. In addition there are both English and Portuguese radio and national print publications, but accurate audience figures are difficult to gauge since the national media survey by ILRES <sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> is conducted in French.
</p><p>Luxembourg is known in Europe for its radio and television stations (<a href="/wiki/Radio_Luxembourg_(French)" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Luxembourg (French)">Radio Luxembourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/RTL_Group" title="RTL Group">RTL Group</a>). It is also the uplink home of <a href="/wiki/SES_S.A." title="SES S.A.">SES</a>, carrier of major European satellite services for Germany and Britain.
</p><p>Due to a 1988 law that established a special tax scheme for audiovisual investment, the film and co-production in Luxembourg has grown steadily.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> There are some 30 registered production companies in Luxembourg.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Luxembourg won an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a> in 2014 in the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Animated_Short_Film" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Animated Short Film">Animated Short Films</a> category with <i><a href="/wiki/Mr_Hublot" title="Mr Hublot">Mr Hublot</a></i>.
</p>
